Doma greets her, asking whether her name was Shinobu or Kanae. Shinobu smiles and tells him that he doesn't have to remember their names, asking him not to address them because it was creepy. Doma compliments Shinobu about the intensity of the poison she used on him, claiming he didn't notice the poison until it had fully circulated his body.
Shinobu meets Doma in the afterlife.
Shinobu explains that Tamayo had assisted in making that poison, expressing her slight frustration that if she could, she would have wanted to kill Doma with a poison she had made herself. Additionally, despite Muzan still being alive, she also expresses faith that one of her peers will kill him as well. Suddenly, Doma claims that his missing heart feels like it is beating, asking Shinobu whether this was love and expressing his surprise that emotions did indeed exist. He then goes on to think that heaven and hell may exist as well, asking Shinobu whether she wanted to go to hell with him. To this, the latter tells him to go to hell already.
Meanwhile, Inosuke stomps on the place where Doma's disintegrated head once was, yelling insults. Growing dizzy, he falls to the ground. He then recalls a conversation he had with Tanjiro and Zenitsu. Inosuke had been yelling that he didn't have a mother. Tanjiro tells him that everyone has to have a mother, to which Inosuke responds that he was abandoned which meant that his mother did not want him. Zenitsu replies that if Inosuke had truly been abandoned, his mother wouldn't have bothered to name him.
Kanao searches for Shinobu's hairpin.
Inosuke retorts back that he doesn't have memories of his mother which was the same as not having one at all. Tanjiro gently reminds him to not speak of his mother that way, stating that his mother must have loved him a lot.Inosuke begins to cry as he remembers his mother. Kanao, on the other hand, looks for Shinobu's hair clip, noting her inability to see clearly from her right eye. She realizes her own hairclip, formerly Kanae's, is now broken, to her sadness. Kanao apologizes to her older sister and recalls the time when Kanae had died; she had been unable to cry at that time, bothering her greatly.
Kanao had been making excuses inside her heart. Being born into an abusive household where crying would result in a punishment, she had been used to holding back her emotions; however, no one at that time blamed her. Kanao finds Shinobu's butterfly hairclip and clutches it to her chest, when she feels the apparitions of Shinobu and Kanae softly patting her head and telling her she did well.
Shinobu reunited with Kanae in the afterlife.
Kanao looks up only to find they weren't there. Shinobu reunites with her sister and her parents in the afterlife. In the pond, holding both her adoptive sisters' hairpins, Kanao begins to cry.
After losing consciousness following his battle, Tanjiro has his rest interrupted by the scent of something burning. He awakens to find Giyu beside him, patched up and stoking a small fire with his katana. As Tanjiro asks if his katana is chipped, Giyu explains that he had tried to stop the bleeding of his wounds, but when that failed he resorted to cauterizing his wounds instead, which unsettles Tanjiro. He also notes that if the cut on his own arm also doesn't stop bleeding, he can cauterize for him as well, though Tanjiro politely refuses the offer. Giyu asks if the bone in his arm is alright, to which Tanjiro answers that it is only a bruise.
Mitsuri and Obanai encounter Nakime.
The Hashira solemnly remarks that their battle was only the beginning, with the final target being Muzan, and they may have to battle Upper Two or One next. The two are interrupted by a Kasugai crow announcing that Shinobu, Kanao, and Inosuke have jointly defeated Upper Two, much to their surprise; Tanjiro asks the crow if the two are alright, who answers they mostly are. He is amazed by their victorious and the realization they are closing in on Muzan. Elsewhere, Mitsuri locates Nakime and discovers her rank of Upper Four. Obanai is surprised by this, knowing that Muichiro and the others had already defeated Upper Four and correctly believing the new demon is a replacement.
Knowing Shinobu was younger than her and still risked her life to do her best, Mitsuri vows to do the same, only to be caught by Nakime and thrown aside by a slamming door. Obanai reacts and catches the Love Hashira, who is embarrassed to have acted so hastily. Obanai explains that as they don't know Nakime's ability, they must analyze her first, but the two nearly fall again when Nakime summons a door beneath them. They catch the door frame in time to save themselves, but Mitsuri is cut off by consecutive opening doors while Obanai faces multiple columns attempting to crush him. Mitsuri is caughtby a column and nearly crushed when she slices it apart in the nick of time.
Confident she has recognized her opponent's patterns, Mitsuri tries again to attack Nakime, but the Biwa Demon summons a new door to take Mitsuri away from her, sending the disappointed Hashira falling again. Obanai closes in on Nakime and uses Serpent Breathing, Second Form: Venom Fangs of the Narrow Head, but the demon reacts by pushing herself away atop another column. He remarks that while not deadly, her Blood Demon Art is instead irritating and could prove a long and troublesome fight. Mitsuri on the other hand has narrowly saved herself by grabbing onto a wooden ledge.
The Mist Hashira comes face to face with Upper Rank One.
Together, Gyomei and Muichiro run through the castle in search of Muzan. But just as Gyomei tells him to not let his guard down, Muichiro is pushed away by a sliding column to the side. The Mist Hashira orders the Stone Hashira to pay him no heed as the column slams through a wooden wall, sending Muichiro into a vast hall of pillars and walls. Inside, Kokushibo spots the visitor in his room and remarks that he appears familiar, while Muichiro can barely comprehend he is now facing Upper Rank One.
Muichiro becomes afraid to fight Kokushibo.
Observing Muichiro through the Transparent World, Kokushibo recognizes something within him. In turn, Muichiro notes that Upper One doesn't appear like the other Upper Ranks, describing him as profoundly majestic. He also notes the katana at his side; despite its warped looks, he questions if the demon was once a Demon Slayer as well as a Breathing Style user. Muichiro begins to tremble uncontrollably as Upper One's intimidating aura overwhelms his senses; it is as if his body is refusing to fight, something he never felt in the past. Kokushibo asks his opponent for his name, and upon hearing the Mist Hashira answer him as Muichiro Tokito, the demon claims that the name Tsugikuni had inevitably died out over the centuries.
Confused by his statement, Muichiro listens as Kokushibo explains his human name was Michikatsu Tsugikuni, and that Muichiro is a member of the family left behind by his son, making him Kokushibo's descendant. Muichiro is stunned by the revelation, as well as the fact that Kokushibo is likely a user of the original Breathing Style. However, he puts his mind at ease and stops shaking, facing Upper One with a determined expression. To this, Kokushibo shows admiration to the Mist Hashira's mental fortitude.
Kokushibo dodges Muichiro's attack, identifying him as a Mist Breathing user.
Muichiro suddenly lunges for an attack using Mist Breathing, Second Form: Eight-Layered Mist, but despite the rapid attack, Kokushibo nonchalantly appears behind him, commending him for his usage of Mist Breathing. Muichiro attacks him again, this time with Fifth Form: Sea of Clouds and Haze, but the demon is easily able to evade the form once again. He addresses Muichiro and notes that despite being only fourteen years of age, his technique is highly refined and he possesses the courage to calm himself to attack him. Kokushibo credits this to his blood; despite it thinning out over generations, his cells have remained and proliferated in him.
Hearing this, Muichiro rejects the notion of his ancestry being his strength; he remarks that after hundreds of years, none of his blood is still in him, as the mark appears on his face. As Kokushibo becomes surprised to see it, Muichiro uses Mist Breathing, Seventh Form: Obscuring Clouds and seemingly cloaks himself in mist. Upper One grows impressed, noting that previous Mist Breathing users had never used such a form; Muichiro suddenly aims his blade at his neck, but the demon once more is able to dodge the attack. He commends his seventh form for its unique tempo and the difficulty to read the disturbances in his movement.
Kokushibo attacks Muichiro and severs his hand.
Amazed at the realization Muichiro had likely created the form, Kokushibo remarks that it would be rude of him not to unsheathe his blade. He draws his katana and uses Moon Breathing, First Form: Dark Moon, Evening Palace, severing Muichiro's left hand. The Mist Hashira is stunned by his use of Moon Breathing, realizing that a demon able to use a Breathing Style has speed completely unseen before. Ripping off his left sleeve, Muichiro quickly ties the fabric around his arm to stop the bleeding; Kokushibo commends his spirit to stop the bleeding and immediately go for another attack against him.
The Hashira attempts to use Mist Breathing, Fourth Form: Shifting Flow Slash but Kokushibo catches the katana mid-attack and stabs Muichiro against a pillar with it. The demon asks Muichiro for a chance to transform him into a demon and be of use to Muzan.
Kokushibo stands before Muichiro as he hangs, pinned by his own katana against a pillar. He claims his heart is moved to see a descendant of his, something he never imagined, and reassures the Mist Hashira that his arm will regrow when he becomes a demon. The Upper Rank also believes he is now the only remaining Upper Rank able to fight, and that Muzan will welcome him as well. He proceeds to gently patch Muichiro's arm stump, believing humans to be fragile. However, he nonetheless claims that if he bleeds out and dies, or Muzan does not accept him as a demon, then his death will have always been his ultimate fate as a human.
Kokushibo severs both of Genya's arms.
Having entered the room, Genya sneaks behind a wall as Kokushibo ties a tourniquet for Muichiro's wound, but as he fires his shotgun, the Upper Rank instantly appears behind the Demon Slayer and asks if he agrees with his sentiment. Genya's left arm suddenly falls off as he remains too paralyzed with fear to react. Muichiro screams for Genya, but as the Demon Slayer attempts to draw his wakizashi, his right arm flies from his body; Kokushibo had slashed him so quickly, it appeared as if he never moved his hand. Upper One notices that the Demon Slayer has been eating demons, just as he slashes Genya in the torso; Muichiro frantically attempts to free himself but cannot pull out the katana. Seeing he is still alive despite his grievous wounds, he reminisces on a similar Demon Slayer who lived 300 years ago and how he too ate demons but was killed when Kokushibo beheaded him.
Sanemi arrives in the nick of time.
Genya desperately attempts to crawl towards his severed arm as Kokushibo declares he has no reason to allow an "imitation demon" such as him to live. But as his katana nears Genya's neck, Sanemi suddenly appears, using Wind Breathing, Fourth Form: Rising Dust Storm to push the demon away from Genya. Kokushibo sees he now faces the Wind Hashira as he responds to his assertion: "That's right! And that wind... is gonna wrench your head off!" Genya is shocked to find his older brother before him, who responds by calling him a pathetic brother. He then reveals the reasons he went so far as to kill their own mother was to protect him.
This causes Genya to recall a past conversation he had with Tanjiro, who notes that despite Sanemi loathing the fact he is a Demon Slayer, he never detected any hatred in him. He doesn't need to be afraid of Sanemi and should be free to speak his mind, because he had always loved him. Sanemi shares his hope that Genya would have a home, a family, and grow old; to make up for the things they could never do with their mother and younger siblings, Genya was supposed to get married and have children. "And I would've never let a demon near you." As Genya apologizes to his brother upon hearing his revelation, Kokushibo observes them and remarks about the nostalgic feeling to see brothers as Demon Slayers together.
Sanemi attacks Kokushibo with First Form: Dust Whirlwind Cutter.
Enraged by the Upper Rank's maiming of Genya, Sanemi lunges towards Kokushibo head-on. Upper Rank One slashes at him, but Sanemi ducks down and slides between the demon's legs, attempting to catch his foot. Kokushibo evades the slash by leaping upwards, but Sanemi responds with Wind Breathing, First Form: Dust Whirlwind Cutter; he charges at the Upper Rank as he lands and forces Kokushibo into a clash of blades to stop him from advancing. Muichiro sees the demon has finally drawn his weapon as Sanemi remarks about the katana's repulsive appearance; the blade is covered in numerous twitching eyes.
Kokushibo uses Fifth Form: Moon Spirit Calamitous Eddy.
As the Wind Hashira and Upper Rank One clash blades, the demon unleashes Moon Breathing, Fifth Form: Moon Spirit Calamitous Eddy, creating a rotating ring of slashes and moon-like blades that force his opponent to back away. Noting that Kokushibo is able to repeat the slashes with a swing of his blade, Sanemi goes for a counterattack and meets the demon with Wind Breathing, Third Form: Clear Storm Wind Tree. Kokushibo lauds the Wind Hashira's physicality and technique as being at their peak, while Sanemi silently remarks that the demon's display of skill is giving him goosebumps.
He sees that each of his slashes is enveloped in chaotic crescent blades that change in size and form, making them unpredictable, and he claims to not be surprised that Muichiro was defeated. Unable to ward off any of the attacks completely, he notes that without his own experience, he would have never been able to defend himself. Furthermore, Sanemi is amazed by Kokushibo's use of a Breathing Style; the combination of his speed with the regeneration and physical prowess of being a demon making him an opponent whose power will only climb.
Sanemi and Kokushibo trade blows.
He excitedly claims Kokushibo is a demon worth killing and uses Wind Breathing, Second Form: Claws - Purifying Wind to slash at his demonic katana. Kokushibo swipes away the wind gusts but is met by the Hashira leaping down to slash at his neck. He blocks Sanemi's katana but senses something from underneath, narrowly moving his neck away from the Hashira attempting to use Genya's fallen wakizashi with his foot. The two continue to trade blows as the Hashira matches the Upper Rank's every move with an attack of his own; Kokushibo notices Sanemi is keeping up with him and remarks about its nostalgic feeling.
Kokushibo injures Sanemi with Sixth Form: Perpetual Night, Lonely Moon - Incessant.
As Muichiro and Genya call out to him, Sanemi begins to grow frustrated at his lack of breathing room, noting that he almost died because he narrowly misses the tip of his swing. Kokushibo reminisces on a time during the Sengoku period when he and the Wind Hashira of then would spar together to improve their skills. Using Moon Breathing, Sixth Form: Perpetual Night, Lonely Moon - Incessant, Kokushibo unleashes a frontal wave of slashes and blades, cutting Sanemi across his chest and limbs and additionally slash apart the surrounding pillars. Genya bemoans being unable to see the battle with the pillars and lattice walls obstructing his view.
As Sanemi stand and begins to bleed heavily from his cuts, Kokushibo commends his opponent for holding out until now. But as he warns him that moving will cause his organs to spill, his pulse begins to quicken, much to his confusion. Sanemi laughs to himself as he explains that Marechi to demons is like silver vine to cats. He suddenly attacks Kokushibo again, who stumbles back and staggers from Sanemi's slash as the Wind Hashira becomes excited to see that his blood works on even Upper Rank demons.
Soon after he began hunting demons, Sanemi noticed that his blood was special, as when his mother attacked him, her movements slowed when he began to bleed; he also remarks that after killing her, it was as if the colors of the world had faded. Because he did not know about the Demon Slayer Corps or Nichirin Swords, when he hunted demons, he did so by arming himself with numerous blades, fighting to restrain them before leaving them to burn in the sunlight. He acknowledges that his past efforts were suicidal and what saved him was his blood being able to intoxicate demons.
Sanemi mourning Masachika's death.
One day, he met a Demon Slayer who was also pursuing demons; his name was Masachika Kumeno and it was he who then introduced him to a trainer. Sanemi bitterly remarks about the unfairness of the world as good people would die one after another; during a battle they fought together against Lower Rank One, Masachika was killed and Sanemi went on to be the Wind Hashira.
As Sanemi attacks Kokushibo with Wind Breathing, Sixth Form: Black Wind Mountain Mist, the demon expresses surprise to see him continuing to fight. Acknowledging that previous Hashira he fought would never reach the stage he is at now, he notices Sanemi has stopped the bleeding of his wounds and wonders if he had coagulated his blood using Total Concentration Breathing or if he is flexing his muscles to stop his organs from spilling. Intrigued to see something he had never seen a human do before, Kokushibo then begins to enjoy the slight intoxication of Sanemi's Marechi, claiming it feels pleasant. He dodges a slash to the side and stomps down on Sanemi's katana. Unable to move, Sanemi watches as Kokushibo brings his blade down onto his neck.
The Hashira express their disapproval towards Sanemi's behaviour to Kagaya.
During his first Hashira meeting, Sanemi became angered to see Kagaya Ubuyashiki smile, claiming he did so as others suffered and believing him to be someone who refused to dirty his hands, hiding behind safety as he gave out orders with an unconcerned expression. His first words to the Oyakata, "Well, aren't you something? Hey! Master Ubuyashiki", drew the ire of Gyomei Himejima and Tengen Uzui, while Kanae Kocho sat by concerned. As Gyomei claims that the Wind Hashira does not appear to know how to speak properly, angrily cracking his rosary, Kagaya assuages the Stone Hashira and allows Sanemi to speak his mind. When Kanae spoke, Kagaya reassured the Flower Hashira and remained composed.
Sanemi angrily claims he is sickened by the Oyakata shamelessly using the Corps members as pawns, to be used and thrown away. He accuses Kagaya of not knowing any martial arts as the head of the Demon Slayer Corps, but to Sanemi's astonishment, Kagaya apologizes to him, causing the angered Hashira to stop his tirade. He mentions that he once tried to swing a sword, but it caused his blood pressure to spike and he was unable to do so even ten times. He would have wanted to be a Demon Slayer like him, to be a strong swordsman to protect others, but because it was impossible for him, he apologizes for making him do the hard work.
Kanae reveals Kagaya's devotion to the Demon Slayer Corps.
Sanemi cannot think of a response to his words and notes that the look on Kagaya's face made him think back to his mother; the affection he gave was like a parent towards their own children. He adds that if Sanemi believes they are pawns, then he is one as well; since his replacement has already been chosen, his death would be meaningless. Kagaya acknowledges that this is Sanemi's first meeting and clears up his confusion that he believes himself to be higher than them; everyone simply treats him with respect but he can be free to avoid it if it bothered him.
Instead, Kagaya only requests that he protect the lives of others as a Hashira and he apologizes for summoning him soon after Masachika's death. When Sanemi becomes surprised to hear Kagaya speak his name, Kanae revealed that since becoming Oyakata, Kagaya has memorized the name and background of every fallen member of the Corps. Sanemi is shocked further by this as he himself has forgotten the names of the Demon Slayers he fought beside. Kagaya explains that every member of the Corps has written a will; they are all similar and Masachika's was no different, as he gives it to Sanemi.
Masachika had thought of him as the younger brother he lost, and like Kagaya's own dream, he hoped for a shining future. A wish for loved ones to smile and live happily till their death without their lives cruelly threatened. Even if those loved ones aren't beside them, they must want them to live and survive; as he continues to read Masachika's will, Sanemi begins to think about Genya and tears up.
Kokushibo blocks Sanemi's shotgun blast.
Sanemi blocks Kokushibo's blade with Genya's fallen shotgun and fires at the demon, but to his chagrin, Kokushibo remains unfazed as he blocks the pellets with his katana. Using Moon Breathing, Third Form: Loathsome Moon, Chains, Kokushibo attempts to kill Sanemi once again but finds he has vanished as the dust cloud of his attack settles. He hears something approaching him and remarks that Demon Slayers appear one after another. Hearing this, Gyomei promises that the Demon Slayer Corps will never disappear until every demon is eradicated from the world.
Having arrived just in time to save the Wind Hashira, Gyomei immediately orders him to stitch his wounds as he takes on Kokushibo himself, which Sanemi acknowledges. The Stone Hashira faces Upper One and begins to spin his flail; observing his new opponent through the Transparent World, Kokushibo grows delighted at Gyomei's physicality, remarking that it had been 300 years since he fought a Demon Slayer of his strength. Gyomei begins to spin his flail faster, causing air to rush past Kokushibo as he realizes it is being drawn towards him.
Kokushibo fails to cut through Gyomei's chain.
Gyomei releases his grip and launches the spiked flail, sending it flying towards the demon and narrowly missing his mark. Kokushibo attempts to use his Moon Breathing but is forced to bend backwards and avoid Gyomei's axe, which he threw immediately after his first attack. He attempts again but Gyomei attacks first with Stone Breathing, Second Form: Upper Smash, stomping down on his chain and driving the flail down to his opponent. Kokushibo dodges to the side but the chain wraps around his neck; he fails to cut through the links and is forced to duck down to escape getting strangled, losing a lock of hair in the process as it burns on contact.
He notes that the chain, axe, and flail are all made of pure iron, making it an extremely refined weapon; as his sword is made of his own flesh, it will burn itself on Gyomei's weapon before it will ever break. He notes that iron that has absorbed so much sunlight wasn't discovered during the Sengoku period, when sword smithing was at its peak. Nonetheless, he knows that going into striking range will benefit him; Kokushibo lunges for an attack and swings at Gyomei's neck. To his surprise, he misses completely as Gyomei leaps high above the attack and throws his axe at him, ripping a part of his haori.
Gyomei's Volcanic Rock, Rapid Conquest clashes with Kokushibo's Pearl Flower Moongazing.
As the Stone Hashira continues, Kokushibo is shocked to see someone capable of wielding such a weapon still being able to fight with belying lightness and agility. The chain wraps around Kokushibo's sword and snaps its blade before the demon can move it. The Hashira and the Upper Rank then meet in a head-on clash of techniques; Kokushibo uses Moon Breathing, Second Form: Pearl Flower Moongazing and Gyomei meets this with Stone Breathing, Fourth Form: Volcanic Rock, Rapid Conquest.
In the aftermath, Kokushibo reveals that whenever his blade breaks, it will always heal, rendering attacks against it useless, while Gyomei on the other hand has sustained a cut across the face. Breathing deeply, he remarks that he had wanted to save it for Muzan but if he was to fail now, he will fall back to where he started. Declaring that he has nothing to lose using it, Gyomei flexes his arms and manifests the mark.
Within another part of the Infinity Castle, Kanao and Inosuke leave Doma's water garden and head out, where they are about to reunite with Zenitsu and Murata behind a corner, the latter of which is supporting the former as he awakens from the ordeal from his recent battle.
After enough effort, Muichiro is finally able to pull his katana out from the pillar and extricate himself. Under immense pain, he pulls the blade out from his shoulder, throwing it aside as he keels over and absorbs the pain. Slowly beginning the process of patching himself up, he notes the horrible state his body is under all of his wounds, remarking that he isn't blessed with a physique like Tengen Uzui. Regardless, Muichiro acknowledges he must at least defeat Upper Rank One to lessen the burden of the survivors; if he was going to die, he very well may do so being useful. He picks up his katana and begins to head out, but is called to by Genya before he can fight.
Surprised to see the Demon Slayer still alive, Muichiro hears Genya as he request for him to push his body towards his torso and give him the fallen lock of Kokushibo's hair to eat. He hopes to fight till the end and prevent Sanemi from dying, which Muichiro agrees to.
"Without exception, the marked ones die... before they reach the age of 25."
Noticing the mark on Gyomei, Kokushibo remarks about his situation being unfortunate. When Gyomei questions him on this, the demon notes that based on his appearance, Gyomei is 27 years of age. The Stone Hashira presses him on what he means and Kokushibo reveals that anyone who awakens the mark will die before the age of 25. Even when it manifests and increases his power, it will merely reduce his lifespan in exchange; being past the age of 25, he will likely die soon during the night. He asks if he will lament that the body and techniques he has refined his entire life will fade with his death, to which Gyomei replies that he does not; everyone is aware of the fate of being marked.
Yet it does not matter to him if it appeared or not; being in the Demon Slayer Corps already means he has no guarantee of seeing the next day. He questions if he should try cling to his life already knowing his fate and believes one cannot become a Hashira with such half-hearted conviction, before declaring that Kokushibo's insult to his existence is making him seethe with rage. An unimpressed Kokushibo replies he was not speaking about his life; he explains that by becoming a demon, he can preserve his body and techniques, calling him foolish for not understanding him. Gyomei retorts there is nothing to understand; the Demon Slayers are proud to live and die as humans, and he demands the demon stop taking his own ideas as the supreme beliefs to force onto others.
He then adds that he sensed a lie whilst they were talking, and that someone must have lived past the age of 25 whilst bearing the mark. This causes Kokushibo to pause; Gyomei proudly claims he is shaken by his taunt as Upper One angrily attempts to kill him by slashing his neck. The Stone Hashira blocks the attack with his chains and they resume battle once more.
The Wind Hashira awakens the mark.
Hiding behind a wall, Sanemi has finished stitching his wounds; he stands up and begins breathing heavily as the mark manifests on his face. Kokushibo and Gyomei trade blows until Sanemi joins the battle and goes on the offensive. As Kokushibo remarks that every Hashira of their generation is seemingly marked, he sees the Wind Hashira duck to the side as Gyomei's flail flies towards him, followng by Sanemi slashing at his feet and forcing the demon away. He realizes that the two are coordinating their attacks despite the two different Breathing Styles and the battle's fast tempo; Sanemi remarks he is glad to have undertaken Hashira Training with him.
After being fed the lock of Kokushibo's hair, Genya begins to breathe heavily and convulse as Muichiro calls out to him in worry. His arm reattaches as an eerie voice rings in his head; Genya questions who the voice belongs to as he sees that his torso has already reconnected itself and he continues to heal at a rapid rate. Noting that all this came from eating just a lock of hair, he wonders just how concentrated Upper Rank One's blood truly is. As his circulation accelerates, he sees there is also the broken piece of the demon's katana, but the voice rings inside him again, asking Kokushibo for how many Hashiras he has killed and warning him not to let them near yet. Realizing he is hearing Muzan's voice, he begins to wonder what will happen to him next if his advancement as a demon continues.
The Wind and Stone Hashira continue to attack Upper Rank One.
As he continues to fight the Stone and Wind Hashira, Kokushibo surmises that even amongst their peers, Gyomei and Sanemi are likely the strongest fighters. He makes emphasis on Gyomei; a Demon Slayer of unparalleled physicality irrespective of his blindness. Furthermore, his weapon is particularly well-crafted; by causing vibrations in the chain, Gyomei is able to accurately read his surroundings. Deciding he will destroy Sanemi's katana first, Kokushibo determines he can strike it on its side to shatter it easily, but Sanemi intercepts the slash and drives Kokushibo's katana into the floor. Seeing his reflexes are still building up, Kokushibo lunges back to avoid a slash that cuts off some of his hair.
Despite his mark empowering him, the demon still believes the Wind Hashira shouldn't be able to fight with all his wounds, yet his movements are only accelerating and becoming more precise. Gyomei suddenly appears in front of him and slashes his axe upwards, cutting off Kokushibo's ear. Sanemi follows through with this by performing Wind Breathing, First Form: Dust Whirlwind Cutter, cutting between them to separate Kokushibo. Together, Sanemi and Gyomei use Wind Breathing, Seventh Form: Gale, Sudden Gusts and Stone Breathing, First Form: Serpentinite Bipolar, ripping off Kokushibo's kimono. As they leap away and land, they immediately rush in for another attack, attempting to go for his head.
Gyomei and Sanemi are injured by Kokushibo.
However, Kokushibo merely stands and encourages them to attack. Sanemi and Gyomei are suddenly covered in numerous slashes before they can get close; Gyomei questions how he managed to attack at range and watches as Kokushibo reveals his katana, now greatly extended and sporting three new cutting edges along its main blade. The demon claims they merely shredded his kimono, "not even enough to kill an infant", and he remarks that after killing the two, everyone will be dispatched with ease.
As Genya ties Muichiro's sword to his remaining hand, Sanemi is narrowly hit by Kokushibo's attack and loses his index and middle fingers on his right hand. Cursing his inability to react to the demon's strike, Sanemi notes that if Gyomei had not diverted the attack's trajectory with his chain, he would have lost both of his arms. The more injuries he sustains, the slower he becomes until he is reduced to being a burden in battle; additionally, his Marechi blood is no longer affecting Kokushibo despite initially working on him. Most concerning is how Kokushibo is able to wield such an immense weapon at incredible speeds, questioning if he could even dodge the next attack or slash the sword to pieces.
Viewing the battle from a Kasugai crow wearing Yushiro's talisman, Kuina Ubuyashiki becomes startled by the turn of events and asks Kiriya if they should send more Hashira to fight Upper Rank One, noting that Tanjiro and Giyu are available. As she and Kanata anxiously wait for an answer, Kiriya decides against it and insists that Tanjiro and Giyu continue towards Muzan instead; he reaffirms his belief in Gyomei, Sanemi, Muichiro, and Genya to defeat Upper One without fail.
Kokushibo uses Moon Breathing, Eighth Form: Moon-Dragon Ringtail.
Kokushibo raises his weapon and unleashes Moon Breathing, Seventh Form: Mirrors of Misfortune, Moonlit, launching powerful long-range slashes at the two Hashira. Though Sanemi and Gyomei barely dodge them, the latter noting that the attack possesses twice the demon's normal attack range, Kokushibo follows through with Eight Form: Moon-Dragon Ringtail; a wide-arcing slash enveloped in crescent blades that cuts Sanemi numerous times. Sanemi curses the situation; he cannot aim for his head since he cannot get close, and with the demon's speed, he can only ward off his attacks defensively, which still take his full effort to do so. Kokushibo uses Ninth Form: Waning Moonswaiths to separate Sanemi from Gyomei, causing a large cut in the Wind Hashira's back.
Kokushibo uses Drilling Slashes, Moon Through Bamboo Leaves against Sanemi.
As Sanemi stumbles, Gyomei calls out to him; he orders Gyomei to ignore him as Kokushibo uses Tenth Form: Drilling Slashes, Moon Through Bamboo Leaves, launching sawblade-like projections that close in on Sanemi. Suddenly, the Wind Hashira is pushed away from the attack as the Mist Hashira grabs hold of him; Muichiro tells Sanemi he won't let him die as he can still use both of his arms. Watching the battle from behind cover, Genya questions if he can be useful in battle or if Kokushibo will simply slash through his torso again. Seeing Sanemi and Muichiro struggling, he promises to not let Sanemi die and to not fail now. As he thinks about Gyomei and Muichiro, he is anguished by his weakness and wishes he was as strong as the Hashira, and the more he wishes to save them, the more hesitant he becomes to act.
Afraid of failing to be of any use and save his friends, Genya asks why he had to be so weak, only to recall a previous chat with Tanjiro. Tanjiro had encouraged him by stating that the weakest amongst a group of people has the most potential. When he fought Upper Rank Six, it was because he was weak that he changed the tides of battle. Surpassing enough people means an opponent will categorize them into the strong and focus on being vigilant against them; if the enemy believes him to be weak, their guard won't be as strong against them and they can deal an unexpected blow; doing that will pave the way to victory.
Remembering Tanjiro's words, Genya steels his resolves to save the Hashira and win, revealing the broken shard of Kokushibo's katana blade. Vowing to not let Sanemi, the Oyakata, or any of his friends die, he swallows the katana blade; despite initially wanting to save it for when he was attacked again, Genya had rejected this and has chosen to act now.
Kokushibo uses Sixteenth Form: Moonbow Half Moon.
Gyomei attempts to perform Stone Breathing, Fifth Form but is intercepted by Kokushibo's Moon Breathing, Sixteenth Form: Moonbow, Half Moon, summoning downward striking slashes around him and Sanemi. The Stone Hashira grows frustrated by how many forms his Breathing Style has, and most concerning is the battle's current direction; Kokushibo is too fast for them, he cannot attack in return, and despite his every actions being based on anticipation, the battle's pace is too fast for him. Making any mistake means Kokushibo will pin him before getting the chance to attack.
As the demon is seemingly predicting the moment he attempts to use a technique, Gyomei wonders what kind of divine power Kokushibo is using, what his eyes see and what he is seeing. Despite the tides of the battle, he resolves to find out, acknowledging that demons are just transformed humans; anything they can do, humans can as well, and he declares that his blind eyes can see a person's true nature, never to be misled.
Gyomei sees into the Transparent World.
As they continue, Gyomei watches Kokushibo performing an attack, and to his shock, he can perceive his pulse and see through his bones and muscles for a moment. At the same time, Muichiro resolves to get inside the demon's attack range; if he can slow down Upper Rank One's movements for even a second, it will enable Sanemi and Gyomei to behead him. Having lost an arm and with the bleeding continuing to worsen, he does not have much time left and pushes himself to act whilst he can move. Suddenly Gyomei yells out Sanemi's name, and simultaneously, all three Hashira charge towards Kokushibo; Muichiro realizes that the other Hashira are adjusting to his plan.
Muichiro stabs Kokushibo, losing his left leg.
Seeing this, Kokushibo remarks they have no option left but a frontal assault, which he can use to wipe out the three all at once. Using Moon Breathing, Fourteenth Form: Catastrophe, Tenman Crescent Moon, he envelops the area before him in swaths of large, rotating slashes covered in crescent blades. Muichiro pushes himself to squeeze between the gaps of the attack, while Sanemi resorts to ducking beneath the slashes instead. Gyomei suddenly throws a bead from his rosary, hitting Kokushibo's hand. Though it doesn't harm him, he questions if he threw it at the moment he swung his chain and how it got past his vision.
Kokushibo then bends back to avoid Sanemi's Dust Whirlwind Cutter but has his right arm destroyed by Gyomei's flail instantly afterwards. As he heals his arm and attempts to determine how Gyomei slipped past his view, his torso is unexpectedly stabbed by Muichiro, who loses his left leg and is slashed in the neck while doing so. However, his carotid artery isn’t harmed and allows Muichiro to keep fighting. Kokushibo questions how the wounded Muichiro slipped past his attacks; at first he believes it was due to Gyomei’s bead slowing him down, but he soon realizes that Muichiro’s eyes now see the same world as he is.
He also determines that Gyomei too is seeing through the Transparent World; though he only began using it in the middle of the fight, the Stone Hashira has already began fighting while taking his vision into account, manipulating his blood flow to disturb his attack pattern. Despite the unexpected developments of the battle, Kokushibo remains confident as none of their blades have reached his neck; if he can understand their plan, it will fall apart quickly. As he raising his katana to perform Moon Breathing’s sixteenth form, Muichiro resolves to hold on no matter what happens to him.
Kokushibo blocks Genya's shot.
Genya appears from behind cover, his eyes now red and yellow like Kokushibo’s and bearing a mark on his head. He recalls Muichiro’s previous words allowing him to shoot at Kokushibo despite being in the bullets’ path, to pay him no heed anymore; if he can stop Kokushibo from moving, he must shoot without hesitation. Pointing his now altered shotgun, Genya fires at Upper One, who reacts by slashing away the bullets.
Genya's Blood Demon Art of trees ensnares Kokushibo.
Despite deflecting Genya's shot with his blade, Kokushibo sees the pellets have redirected and punched into his body. He notices Genya and sees that along with his new appearance, his shotgun is changing form. Suddenly, the pellets in his body begin to soak in his blood, sprouting into giant trees that prevent him from moving; Genya's own Blood Demon Art, and he was able to achieve so by absorbing his hair and the piece of his blade. Now trapped and unable to fight, Kokushibo watches as the Hashira all converge on him at once; he is disturbed by the feeling, that of his life being threatened and his core seizing up. His composure crumbles in a detestable way as it brings back memories from 400 years ago.
That day, Kokushibo was out at night during a blood moon when he saw something he could hardly believe. His brother had approached him, now appearing old and decrepit; it had been 60 years since they last met, meaning Yoriichi was now in his 80s. He had thought it to be impossible and questioned how he still lived. He began asking how he survived given the curse of the mark supposedly killing him before the age of 25, when Yoriichi tearfully spoke and extended his sympathies towards him. "The old and ugly creature that was once my little brother... had pity for me", Kokushibo had remarked. Despite this, he himself was not angry; for 60 years he had been an eyesore in his life, but the voice calling out to him was hoarse.
"I was confused... by my own unexpected unrest."
The sensation of seeing Yoriichi crying before him, who he had known was emotionless for most of his life, gave him a feeling of confusion; he was confused by why he was unsettled to see him. He knew then that he had to kill Yoriichi and remove the last fragment of his life as a human. He was an old man past his prime, but he remained a Demon Slayer, someone he had to kill. However, Yoriichi's sentimentality disappeared as he reached for his katana and took his stance. Instantly, Kokushibo felt as if rocks had appeared on his shoulders as the weight of the air increased with his intimidating aura; Yoriichi had no openings in his stance.
Yoriichi slitting Kokushibo's neck.
His brother told him he was about to strike, but before Kokushibo could react, Yoriichi had already slit his throat. Boiling with rage, he turns to face him and asks why he had to be the special one. Despite bearing the mark, he continued to live, and the technique he displayed demonstrated his power and speed had not waned in the slightest. The vivid memories of his 60 year long grudge returned. Like jealousy burning his bones, his existence was to transcend the laws of the natural world and live like he was favored by the gods. Declaring that he hated and wanted to kill him, Kokushibo prepared for the next strike despite knowing it would kill him.
His speed, which had pushed Muzan into a corner, was nothing short of godly. He waited with a feeling of dread and unrest, as if his insides would burst to flames, but his wait was for nothing as Yoriichi never struck again; he had died standing up, his katana impaled in the ground.
As he observed Yoriichi's dead body, Kokushibo remarked that had he taken one more breath, he would have lost. For centuries, he continued to bear the indignity of never facing an honourable death; with Yoriichi's death, he will never see an honorable death. With the loss of the greatest swordsman to have ever lived, Kokushibo decided he could never lose again; he chose to continue winning, "...until... I became ugly... like this."
Kokushibo releases crescent blades from his body to free himself, mortally wounding Muichiro and Genya.
Kokushibo howls in fear of his life and releases powerful slashes from within his body without warning, narrowly missing Sanemi and Gyomei but cutting Muichiro's body below the waist and splitting Genya down the middle. Numerous katana blades cover his body; Muichiro is aghast at how he attacked so ferociously without swinging his sword, just by the sheer number of blades on him. Only moments ago, he was cornered, yet the monster that is Kokushibo is now pushing them on the brink again and he scrambles to find a way to help before his death. Nearby, the weakened Genya mutters of his hope to protect everyone regardless.
Sanemi and Gyomei attack Kokushibo together; Muichiro realizes they intend to fight him to the death, yet he cannot let them die. Muzan still awaits them and he seeks to protect the two. As Kokushibo prepares another attack, thinking quickly, the Mist Hashira grips his imbedded katana with all his might, causing it to turn bright red. Upper One feels as if his body is stiffening and his insides are set alight. Seeing him distracted allows Sanemi to land a blow on Kokushibo's neck, but the demon's durability proves too much and he can barely induce a cut in his skin. Genya, realizing his flesh bullets are still inside Kokushibo, sees the demon is distracted completely by the three Hashira.
Muichiro's blade turn bright red, burning Kokushibo.
He summons then once more and immobilizes Kokushibo completely again. Enraged by his predicament, Kokushibo prepares to release his crescent blades to kill Genya, but finds the attack cannot be released from his katana. Gyomei's flail hits home on his neck and back, burning Kokushibo as he screams in pain. Seeing his opponent's tremendous durability, Gyomei employs his axe and swings from underneath, pinning the Upper Rank's neck between both weapons. Kokushibo realizes his Blood Demon Art cannot be summon as the trees inside him are sucking his blood, and the pain in his body making him seize is coming from a red blade, similar to Yoriichi.
Upper Rank One is beheaded.
He flashes back to a time when he spoke with Yoriichi when they were both Demon Slayers; he had asked him on his plan to be succeeded. Nobody could compare to them, and because their Breathing Styles could not be taught to anyone, the techniques they have mastered will fade into history. Yoriichi spoke to his brother:
"My brother... we are not that great. We are merely a fragment of humankind's long, long history. At this moment, those whose talent will surpass ours are uttering their first cries. They may come to reach the same place. There is no need to worry. We can draw the curtain of life closed without unease at any time. Does that not exhilarate you? Brother?"
As Kokushibo reflects on his brother's words, Sanemi lands a powerful blow onto Gyomei's flail; the impact causes both weapons to turn bright red. As Upper Rank One's head finally falls from his shoulders, his brother's words ring in him once more. "Someday the children now being born will surpass us and ascend to even greater heights."
Kokushibo remarks about feeling disturbed whenever he saw Yoriichi smile; when they spoke about how the various Breathing Styles he taught had no successor, he smiled because he saw the situation with optimism. Kokushibo was proud of the fact that his generation alone was special, feeling sickened with disgust and irritation by his brother's baseless optimism for the future.
He curses the persistence of the Hashira as he recalls his memories of Yoriichi; the children of the future don't release their blades even when dismembered (Muichiro), they can use Blood Demon Arts as humans (Genya), they refuse to bleed to death as they are continually cut down (Sanemi), and they grow and surpass their limit at a rate that even matches demons (Gyomei). They do not use Sun Breathing, yet are able to turn their weapons bright red. He questions what he found amusing about such a future and claims that just the thought of losing is making him boil over with rage.
Upper Rank One vows to never again lose, even after a decapitation; with this, he stops the bleeding in his neck. Gyomei sees this and orders Sanemi to attack with everything he has and drive Kokushibo into a corner; Muichiro and Genya have given their lives and he refuses to let them die in vain. A tearful and enraged Sanemi acknowledges and promises to shred the demon into nothing. Using Wind Breathing, Eighth Form: Primary Gale Slash, Sanemi surrounds Kokushibo and slashes his body, while Gyomei performs Stone Breathing, Fifth Form: Arcs of Justice and strikes the area around the demon to trap him. Kokushibo slashes off Muichiro's dead body with his hand and attempts to pull his katana from out of his body.
Kokushibo's monstrous new form.
Declaring he will not crumble, he surmises he can still heal; with Muichiro and Genya's deaths, the bright red blade and Blood Demon Art of trees will fade and allow him to conquer death from decapitation. The Wind and Stone Hashira attack together but Kokushibo suddenly vanishes, before appearing behind them. The demon has regenerated his head, but his unstable regeneration has caused him to attained a grotesque, monstrous form. Sanemi is livid to see him regrow a head but Gyomei realizes his body will be weakened because of it. Seeing he does not heal as quickly as Muzan, they aim for his head again. Proud of his efforts, Kokushibo sees he has finally defeated death by being decapitated, leaving only the sun as the last option to kill him.
But as he boasts that he will never lose again, he sees his reflection in Sanemi's blade. Kokushibo is disgusted by his new form, before he suddenly hears a young Yoriichi's voice behind him. "My brother, is your dream to become the strongest samurai in the land? I want to be like you. I... want to become the second strongest samurai." He questions if what he appears now is truly the look of a samurai, if it was something he really wanted. In that moment, where Muichiro had stabbed him in the body begins to crumble to ash, distracting Kokushibo long enough for Gyomei to destroy his head once more.
Unable to attack, Kokushibo's body is destroyed Gyomei and Sanemi overwhelm him.
As Sanemi follows through with a ripping attack to shred his body, Kokushibo desperately attempts to use his Blood Demon Art but is unable to. As his body crumbles faster, he tries to believe he can still regenerate but sees Yoriichi's wizened visage before him, pitying the Upper Rank for his state. As Sanemi and Gyomei relentlessly destroy his body, Kokushibo remarks of his unwillingness to accept defeat, despite being decapitated, dismembered, and crushed by his enemies. He has been living in disgrace for hundreds of years just to die now, and he wonders if his fear of death had caused him to become a monster that eats humans.
"Did I become this miserable creature because I didn't want to die? No. Yoriichi... I just wanted to be you."
In reminiscence of his brother, Kokushibo remarks that anyone who has not felt jealousy is lucky to have never done so, that they have never met someone like Yoriichi, someone he believes was always favored by the gods. To him, it was as if Yoriichi was the very sun, shining so brightly and fiercely he consumed everything around him.
Yoriichi's mother sought to protect him for her husband.
During the time they were born, twins were considered a bad omen as they caused a struggle between them for succession. Additionally, Yoriichi was born with a large mark on his forehead, causing their father to consider having him killed. When their mother heard this, she became deeply enraged and grabbed him, needing to be restrained by their servants. Instead, it was decided that Yoriichi would be sent to live in the temples when he turned ten, adopting a life of priesthood. Their upbringing were polar opposites; everything from their rooms, clothes, education, and food were segregated from each other. Yoriichi was also secluded in a small room of their house by himself.
Michikatsu believed Yoriichi's poor treatment was why he constantly held onto their mother at all times, and he subsequently saw his twin as pitiful, nothing else. Despite this, behind their father's back, he gave his brother a flute he had made, knowing he would notice being given any of his own belongings. However, Yoriichi never once smiled, not doing so even as an infant; furthermore, he did not speak until he was seven and was thought to be deaf. The moment he realized Yoriichi could speak was when Michikatsu was practicing his swordsmanship, while Yoriichi stood silently in the shade. Seeing him alone was an eerie feeling when he suddenly heard his voice; he asked Michikatsu if he dreamt of being the greatest samurai in the land.
Michikatsu unnerved by Yoriichi smiling for the first time.
He was stunned as he never imagined he could speak, yet he spoke to him with such clarity, he dropped his wooden sword in shock. As Yoriichi proclaimed he would be the second greatest in deference of him, Michikatsu noted that Yoriichi would soon turn ten and become a monk. Whether he realized it or not, Yoriichi then smiled at his brother, which unnerved him. He believed someone who always clung to their mother would never give their life as a samurai. Regardless, the next time he trained, Yoriichi stood closer in the hope of receiving some instructions, upon which one of his trainers gave him a bamboo sword to humor him. After instructing him to hold it and take a proper stance, the trainer took his own stance.
In an instant, Yoriichi lands three strikes on the trainer.
Yoriichi then suddenly lunged forth and struck the trainer with three quick blows, before a fourth knocks the man down to the ground. Michikatsu was astonished as he never once was able to land a blow, yet Yoriichi had landed four in an instant; a seven year old child causing a grown man to develop fist-sized welts on his neck, chest, stomach, and foot. After that, Yoriichi decided he no longer wanted to become a samurai as he was uncomfortable at the thought of striking others. Michikatsu pressed him for the secret of his strength, and eventually, Yoriichi said that before taking a strike, he observed his opponent's skeletal alignment, muscular contractions, and blood flow.
At first, Michikatsu did not understand his answer, and it wasn't until later on when he realized Yoriichi could see into the inside of living things. The mark he bore gave him extraordinary vision as well as matching physical might. The brother he had looked down on for so long suddenly surpassed him in every way, yet Yoriichi had stated he would rather play suguroku and fly kites with him than talk about swordsmanship. Michikatsu himself sought mastery of the sword, doing so with relentless training under the belief that he could become strong by putting all his effort into it. Yet compared to Yoriichi, he was at a turtle's pace. He was given the gifts, but Yoriichi did not pursue swordsmanship at all. Irrespective of his skill, he saw it as less worthy of his time than playing games.
Michikatsu became the unfavored son, kept in Yoriichi's room.
Soon after, Michikatsu was then confined to Yoriichi's room as his trainer informed his father. Yoriichi was going to be the successor to his father while he would become a monk, his dream of being a samurai shattered. One night, Yoriichi came to his room in the early morning to inform him of their mother's death, which shocked Michikatsu. Before he could speak, Yoriichi apologized for the few details, asking he instead speak to their retainer for the details, as he was to depart for the temple soon. Surprised by this, he watches as Yoriichi reveals the flute he gave him; he thinks about the flute as if it were him and he will cherish it, never losing heart no matter how far apart they were.
Michikatsu grows jealous of Yoriichi.
Michikatsu became disgusted by this; Yoriichi treasured a crude gift and smiled about it; unable to understand why he was so happy about it, he couldn't reply back. Yoriichi then bowed his head and departed their household, carrying only a bag with him. Some time after, Michikatsu began to read his mother's diary; Yoriichi had realized his role as the successor and sought to leave before it could happen. It also seemed as if Yoriichi had known about their mother's illness as she had been suffering from the left of her body for years before her death.
It is then that he realized whenever Yoriichi clung to their mother, he doing so to support her left side, not because he was feeble or weak like he thought. The realization causes Michikatsu to be struck with jealousy, tearing his mother's diary as he curses his twin brother.
As Michikatsu begs Yoriichi to die and wishes he was never born, believing his existence was in defiance of nature, he listens to the fate of his brother. His father had sent an envoy to the temple and retrieve him, though he was not there. Yoriichi disappeared seemingly without a trace; whether it was a landslide, a bear, or being kidnapped, his wish had come true. For the next ten years, he lived peacefully; Michikatsu eventually got married and had children, but he recalls it was as if time had slowed to a crawl.
Yoriichi saves Michikatsu from a demon.
One fateful day, his camp was attacked by a demon, leaving his fellow samurai dead and him as the sole survivor. As the passage of time began to accelerate once again, he had an unexpected encounter. Yoriichi appeared and instantly struck down the demon; he was different to the person he was as a child and had completely mastered the sword, easily defeating inhuman opponents. Seeing Yoriichi again destroyed the serenity of his life, and as his stomach boiled with jealous hatred, he watched his twin kneel before and apologize for his lateness allowing his subordinates to be killed.
Now seeing Yoriichi was a seemingly faultless individual, Michikatsu decided to take his skills for his own no matter the costs. He abandoned his family and took the path of a Demon Slayer. Duriing this time, Yoriichi sought to teach his peers about swordsmanship and breathing techniques, but when none of them could match him, he altered the styles to suit them personally. This gave rise to the various Breathing Styles, and subsequently, as the Demon Slayers' power rose, so did the number of people who gained the mark like Yoriichi.
The Sengoku era Hashira discuss the deaths caused by the mark.
Eventually, Michikatsu attained a mark as well that was similar to his twin's, but in the end, he could not use Sun Breathing. Instead, he used a derivative that eventually came to be known as Moon Breathing. He had thought he could match Yoriichi's power by training, and as he languished in frustration, those who gained the mark began to die in droves. They soon discovered the mark merely exchanged a user's lifespan for the given power, and as such, the Golden Era of Demon Slayers would end; Michikatsu was subsequently left with no future or the neccessary training to surpass Yoriichi.
It was then that he encountered Muzan Kibutsuji; the Demon King tempted him by explaining he could live forever, and by doing so, he could master his Breathing Style and Muzan would gain a demonic swordsman from it. Given the choice, Michikatsu realized the path he truly sought had been laid before and he could be free of all his fetters. Yet, when Yoriichi encountered Michikatsu again 60 years later, it was a reminder that not all his shackles were gone. His twin who transcended the laws of nature had appeared before him and died, thereby defeating him once more and robbing him of victory forever.
An angered Kokushibo slashes Yoriichi's body in half.
No one, not even Muzan, could defeat, and as he demands to know why he had to always make him feel miserable, Kokushibo slashes Yoriichi's body in half. To his shock, he sees the flute he gave him when they were children and recalls his words. "I think of this flute you gave me... as you." Kokushibo attempts to force his hatred on him as he tears up at the sight of it. "Just seeing your face makes me sick. Just hearing your voice makes me so angry my head hurts."
Kokushibo laments that even after hundreds of years passing, the face he had wanted to forget the most appeared the vivid; he had long forgotten the faces of his parents, his wife, and children, yet his continued to stay clear. Yoriichi was the sun, and around him, humanity would have no path but to yearn and reach out for it as they writhed in agony until they faded. As the last portions of Kokushibo's body begin to fade, Upper One laments that he could never hold onto anything at all. Having abandoned his home, his wife and children, his humanity, and even after striking down his descendant and forgoing becoming a samurai, it was still never enough.
The death of Upper Rank One.
He recalls Yoriichi once stating that those who master their paths would all reach the same place, yet he did not and he couldn't see the world he saw. Even after Yoriichi's death, when he and Muzan killed every Demon Slayer who knew Sun Breathing and its forms, the style continues to live. Finally, as Kokushibo fades into nothing, leaving behind the flute he once gave to Yoriichi and has now kept with him for 400 years, he questions the entirety of his existence.
"Why could I not leave anything behind? Why could I not become someone? Why are we so different? Why in the world was I ever born? Tell me... Yoriichi."
As Kokushibo disintegrates entirely and is dragged down to Hell against his will, Sanemi continues to blindly attack the spot where he last remained. Gyomei orders him to relent as the demon has stop regenerating, but resorts to grabbing the Wind Hashira by force to make him stop. As he explains they have finally defeated Upper Rank One and the battle has finished, Sanemi collapses in his hold, surprising him to see he was still moving despite being unconscious. After laying him to rest on the ground, he thinks of Muichiro and Genya.
Nearby, Genya weakly calls out to him, asking for Sanemi and Muichiro's condition. Gyomei reassures the Demon Slayer that he and Sanemi are alright; Genya then points his attention to Muichiro, asking him to tend to the Mist Hashira as he will be alright. Surprised to see Genya still alive despite his wounds, he reasons this is due to him eating demons; regardless, Genya's regeneration is wearing off with his blood loss. Believing that placing marechi blood beside him would be beneficial, Gyomei moves the unconscious Sanemi to be with Genya before he tends to Muichiro; Genya is relieved to see his older brother is still alive.
Gyomei, seeing Muichiro has already succumbed to his wounds, removes his haori to cover the lower half of his body. Passionately thanking the Mist Hashira for his efforts to help them win, the Stone Hashira gives his gratitude and respect. For someone so young, he accomplished his goal magnificently, and Gyomei tearfully promises him they will not fail to defeat Muzan, before closing his eyes and asking him to finally rest.
Yuichiro becomes upset to see Muichiro, realizing he too is dead.
Muichiro awakens in the afterlife and sees his twin brother Yuichiro standing before him, but Yuichiro becomes angry and tearfully demands he return to the living world. Muichiro cries as he asks for why he wouldn't praise him for his efforts. Yuichiro instead asks why he would give his life at fourteen years old, believing he should have ran away. When Muichiro claims he couldn't simply abandon his comrades, Yuichiro replies he still shouldn't have died now, believing his death would be for nothing and giving him no reason to be born. Muichiro reminds his twin he died a sorrier death at just eleven years of age, before answering his question. "As for the reason I was born... I know that full well. I... was born to be happy."
Yuichiro and Muichiro embrace, reunited once again.
He confronts Yuichiro by asking if he was ever happy in his life, revealing he was happy to live with his family. When he was alone, he suffered many tragedies, yet he made new friends and was able to smile again as his mind becomes flooded by his happy moments. Asking to know if he had done enough, to refuse running away and risk his life for the sake of his comrades, Muichiro wipes away his tears as he demands Yuichiro to never speak to him harshly again, regardless of what anyone else says. Holding his brother by the shoulders, Yuichiro gently apologizes, acknowledging that he understands his reasoning; he simply did not want to see him dead, as he pulls his twin into an embrace.
As Sanemi opens his eyes, he suddenly screams in horror, causing Gyomei to turn back to see what is happening. Genya begins to disintegrate into ash as Sanemi questions why it is happening; Genya weakly calls out to him and Sanemi pleads with his brother not to worry as he attempts to help him. He apologizes to Sanemi for the time he condemned him during their childhood, believing he always was a trouble to him. Sanemi rejects this and claims he never once was troubled by Genya's actions, pleading that he cannot die before him.
Sanemi grieving Genya's death.
Genya thanks his brother for his protection but Sanemi retorts that he did not; to this, Genya remarks of wanting to protect Sanemi the way he has done to him. They feel the same way being brothers, and after seeing how much he has suffered, Genya only wants to see Sanemi happy and alive. "Because... my big brother... is... the nicest person... in... this world." As the Hashira pleads with the gods to spare his younger brother's life, Genya thanks his older brother for the last time before disintegrating completely.
Holding his clothes, Sanemi begins mourning the death of his brother. Gyomei calmly approaches him and implores the Wind Hashira to soldier on and raise his head, solemnly reminding him that the battle is not over until Muzan is defeated.
Continuing through the Infinity Castle, Tanjiro and Giyu hear the news of Muichiro and Genya's deaths. Tanjiro cries as he remarks that everyone now seems to be dying, yet he pushes aside the pain to focus on the mission. He wills himself to keep going until the end no matter what; as everyone before him, he must go onwards without hesitation. However, he believes himself to be unready to be a successor; after reading Senjuro's letter, he knows that Hinokami Kagura has 13 forms, yet he only knows 12. Regardless, he must defeat Muzan for everyone's sake.
Kiriya realizes they have run out of time; the Demon Slayers will not be able to reach Muzan to save Tamayo and he will return. He then receives news that the first squad of Demon Slayers has arrived at his location, with a second squad on the way. The Oyakata warns them not to engage Muzan and wait for the Hashira to arrive, but the squad is already attempting to cut the cocoon down. This fails, and they try to cut the flesh attached to the walls first. A Demon Slayer then receives Kiriya's order to stand down, but another declares they cannot stand by and do nothing, and instead they must do anything to stop him before the Hashira arrive.
Muzan annihilates the first squad of Demon Slayers.
Without warning, the cocoon splits and a transformed Muzan leaps into the air, descending to cut down the leading Demon Slayer before he can even react. In an instant, Muzan kills the Demon Slayers in a bloody flurry of slashes as he leaps instantly between them, the fighters completely unable to stand up to the demon. Kiriya frantically orders them to wait for the Hashira or they will only act as Muzan's food, but the message is received too late as Muzan proclaims they are now all dead. He sees the Kasugai crow acting as Kiriya's mouthpiece and decapitates it.
Muzan remarks that after living for a thousand years, one can lose their sense of taste; being hungry before the attack has allowed him to enjoy the flesh of the Demon Slayers. He mockingly praises Kagaya for providing him with sustenance, and though he does not know his successor to the position of Oyakata, he is greatly impressed by them. He adds that if they were to kneel before him, he would be willing to make them into a demon as his subordinates are all dead. Kiriya then orders the second squadron to fall back and avoid Muzan; if he eats them as well, he will recover his strength.
Muzan kills Tamayo.
Muzan turns his attention to Tamayo in his hand, now left as a crumbling severed head. As he mocks her attempt to poison him with her transformative drug as a failure, Tamayo boldly claims he will go to hell today. The Demon King retorts her threat as countless humans have told him those exact words throughout his existence, and it still has yet to come true. With tears welling in her eyes, Tamayo finally pleads with Muzan to give back her husband and children. In response, Muzan coldly remarks, "Die and join those relatives you killed", before crushing the demon's head and absorbing her remains.
Muzan massacres the second squad of Demon Slayers.
Elsewhere in the castle, Yushiro is suddenly racked with pain and collapses on the floor; as Takeuchi sees him and asks if he is alright, he can only claw at the floor in agony as he realizes Tamayo has been killed. Muzan soon locates the second squad of Demon Slayers and kills them, meeting no resistance as he uses his potent abilities to annihilate the troops entirely. Kiriya demands they retreat and asks if Giyu is yet to arrive there. Being informed the Water Hashira is in the other direction, Kiriya panics at the thought of Muzan massacring the Demon Slayers, leaving Tamayo's sacrifice in vain as he recovers his strength.
Deriding his fallen Upper Ranks as useless, Muzan declares that he alone will kill all of the Demon Slayers tonight.
Kuina slaps her brother to snap him from his catatonic state.
Kiriya enters a state of shock at the realization that his mistake has resulted in much of the Demon Slayers being slaughtered. He freezes in his indecision, and he cannot hear Kuina calling to him as he begins to think that the efforts made to kill Muzan over the centuries will be futile because of him. With no options, Kuina forcefully slaps her brother across the face, much to Kanata's shock; she tells him to remain strong and to give a new order as the battle is not done.
Recalling that his father, grandfather, and the past Oyakatas have also experienced the same immense pressure as him, Kiriya pushes aside his doubts. He orders the Kasugai crows to spread out and close in on Muzan, and to gather the Hashira and remaining Demon Slayers to one location. Before they continue, Kiriya thanks Kanata and Kuina for their help; Kuina acknowledges his recognition of their efforts.
Mitsuri and Obanai receive orders to regroup as Muzan has now returned, shocking the Love Hashira as she realizes they have been stalled the entire time. A similarly frustrated Obanai notes that whilst Muichiro and Genya gave their lives in the attempt to defeat Upper One, he has done nothing in comparison. He sees that while Nakime’s Blood Demon Art is not particularly deadly, she is instead prolonging the battle and preventing them from killing her while doing so. Having stalled two Hashira into doing nothing, Nakime forces Obanai to think of a new plan to allow them to rejoin. Mitsuri questions how she and Obanai can simply leave the Biwa Demon mid-battle, just as someone grabs her by the haori.
Tanjiro and Giyu face a transformed Muzan.
Nakime begins to strum her biwa, the notes echoing within the Infinity Castle as she manipulates the positions of Tanjiro, Giyu, and Muzan into one area. Coming face to face with the Demon King, Tanjiro’s breathing becomes erratic as his mind is flooded by the memories of his dead family, Nezuko, and the deceased Hashira he grew so close to. He trembles with rage as he holds his katana, forcing Giyu to order him to calm down.
Unexpectedly, Muzan remarks about their persistence; he is sick of them and his patience is wearing thin, wondering why they continue to talk about avenging those they loved and asking if just being alive is not enough for them. This enrages Tanjiro and Giyu, but Muzan continues by asking why they care about the loved ones he has killed, believing they should consider themselves lucky and continue with living on.
When Tanjiro questions how Muzan can say something with such indifference, Muzan insists they act as if those loved ones were simply killed by a natural disaster. Whether it is rain, wind, volcanoes, or an earthquake, people do not seek revenge against them, and because the dead cannot return, they should let go of their grudges and continue to live a quiet life. Most people do, and to this end, Muzan believes the Demon Slayers to be abnormal for their refusal to accept their deaths he has caused. “And I’m tired of dealing with you. I just want things to end.”
Tanjiro, having listened to the revelation of Muzan’s monstrous disregard to the lives of humanity, simply mutters one sentence: “Muzan… we… cannot allow you to exist anymore.”
As he faces Muzan head-on, Tanjiro internalizes that he has never felt such coldness towards a living being. His stomach churns with hatred, something he has never experienced before, and the extent of his hatred is pointed directly at the Demon King. Even if they were to behead him, Muzan will not die, and they must find a way to drag him towards sunlight. Regarding the orders they received, he and Giyu must stall Muzan until the other Demon Slayers can arrive and plan a way to extend the battle until the dawn’s arrival; they must ascertain and convey any advantageous knowledge about Muzan to the others. Finally, they must survive long enough to do so as it is only until that point when the true battle starts.
Muzan attacks with his bladed arms and immense speed.
Weaponizing his arms with flesh blades and hooks, Muzan ferociously attacks the Water Hashira and Demon Slayer; he takes a moment to admire his new prowess as he destroys the area around them. Giyu is barely able to block his attack with Water Breathing, Eleventh Form: Dead Calm; he remarks that his arms are as sharp as blades, he can extend them, and he possesses immense speed. Seeing that he cannot dodge Muzan's attacks on instinct alone, Tanjiro decides he must get in close by going past his attacks.
He lunges at the demon and successfully dodges his attack, enabling him to get near; Muzan suddenly throws him off-balance and cuts Tanjiro’s right eye whilst he is downed. As he questions how he was struck, Tanjiro is nearly attacked again but is narrowly saved by Giyu, who explains that they have no need to attack him directly since he is more powerful than an Upper Rank. But with nothing to shield them and no way out of the battle, he also notes the helplessness of their situation.
Tanjiro and Giyu are overwhelmed by Muzan's attacks.
Muzan overhears them and notes that sunlight cannot reach inside the castle, wondering how three Hashira can accomplish this feat. When Tanjiro and Giyu grow shocked by his statement about three Hashira, Muzan reveals that Nakime has already killed Obanai and Mitsuri; sharing his vision with his subordinate, he can see the dead bodies of the Serpent and Love Hashira. The Demon King continues his onslaught and attacks between the two Demon Slayers to separate them.
Tanjiro forces himself to attack as to not burden Giyu; while he dodges the demon’s attacks, he believes that even with one eye, he can smell out the attacks and see into the Transparent World. However, Muzan is attacking too quickly and he cannot maintain his breathing whilst dodging them, leading Tanjiro to get hit by a wall behind him when he cannot see his surroundings. Before Muzan’s arm can hit Tanjiro, Mitsuri bursts through the ceiling behind the demon, shocking him and Giyu.
Obanai orders Tanjiro to fall back.
Using Love Breathing, Sixth Form: Cat-Legged Winds of Love, she attacks Muzan but becomes stunned to see she has not harmed the demon at all. Obanai appears beside Tanjiro and orders him to stay back, seeing he is only an encumbrance in battle. Tanjiro becomes thankful to see him and Mitsuri alive, though Obanai then asks if he could worry about himself instead of others. As Muzan looks on at his unexpected opponents, he questions how they are alive and yells at Nakime about what she is doing.
Yushiro hijacks Nakime's vision, allowing him to control the Infinity Castle himself.
Yushiro, revealing himself to be the one responsible, answers Muzan's question by explaining that he now control her vision. He accuses the demon of committing the gravest sins of the world and demands he kneel in penance for his murder of Tamayo. As the entirety of the Infinity Castle begins to warp and shake violently, Yushiro declares his intentions to force Muzan out into the open.
Mitsuri becomes hesitant to attack Muzan.
Repeating biwa strums begin echoing within the Infinity Castle, changing the landscape of the battlefield rapidly. Mitsuri pushes herself to continue fighting despite the forces of the castle pummelling her, but upon seeing the angered Muzan, she grows frightened, believing him to be scarier than any demon she has faced and wishing Gyomei would arrive soon. She also remarks about Yushiro's perpetual scowl and his plan to pretend that the Hashira were dead becoming futile when Giyu, Obanai, and Tanjiro are all in danger.
Previously, when Yushiro grabbed her, he explained that whilst being a demon, he is on their side. He goes on to inform Mitsuri of his plan to handle Nakime whilst her objective was to run around the demon as a decoy Distracting her will allow him sneak behind and hijack the Biwa Demon's vision, where he can remove Muzan's influence and control her mind, leaving Mitsuri astonished by his abilities. Yushiro plans to trick Muzan into believing the Hashira and other Demon Slayers are dead, giving them time to gather their forces and attack him at once.
Mitsuri nearly slips off a moving column as she surmises that the situation is now a clash of wills between Muzan and Yushiro; though they must attack Muzan to help Yushiro, she believes she could die before it happens as the Infinity Castle becomes erratic and unpredictable. Tanjiro nearly falls through an open door as he attempts to stay close to Muzan and avoid getting separated. Realizing he cannot see Nakime's attacker, Muzan surmises them to be Yushiro and decides to kill him.
Yushiro battles Muzan over control of the Infinity Castle.
As Yushiro attempts to control the Infinity Castle using Nakime, the skin in his hand begin to decay and bleed as Muzan attempts to wrestle control of her; he sees the demon is even attempting to absorb his own cells. As the two clash, Takeuchi sees Yushiro struggling greatling and offers himself to be eaten in order to give him strength, only to be refused by the angered demon. Muzan is then attacked by Giyu and Obanai, using Water Breathing, Fourth Form: Striking Tide and Serpent Breathing, First Form: Winding Serpent Slash to circle around the demon and distract him.
Muzan kills Nakime to stop Yushiro.
Muzan subsequently loses concentration on Nakime, allowing Yushiro to push back his influence and manipulates the castle; he causes the demon to fall through the floor, but as he plummets, Muzan resorts to remotely killing Upper Rank Four. He enacts his curse and destroys Nakime's head; Yushiro realizes the Infinity Castle will collapse with her death and scrambles to control her dying cells and transport everyone outside. As Tanjiro and Obanai lose balance on the column they stand on, he sees destroyed blade and mangled bodies of the Demon Slayers, believing they must have died regretful.
With Yushiro occupied with controlling the castle, Muzan continues his attack against the Demon Slayers, destroying the floor around Mitsuri and Obanai to separate them and cutting Tanjiro in the arm. The castle begins to groan and creak; Obanai remarks that only Muzan will survive if everyone is not outside, while Mitsuri sees the building they stand on is rising. She is nearly struck by Muzan but is saved by Obanai pushing her and a timely throw from Tanjiro, using a fallen Demon Slayer's katana to impale his head. As Muzan curses Tanjiro, the building breaks through the ceiling of the Infinity Castle, causing everyone to be shoved outside into the open.

Kanata reveals dawn is still 90 minutes away.
Staring at the open sky and his surroundings, Tanjiro senses that while they are outside the Infinity Castle, the situation has become more dire. Kiriya realizes that whilst Muzan has been taken to the surface, they are in the middle of a city, far from where was expected. It had been a tug-of-war between Yushiro and Muzan over control of the castle, and while not ideal, he notes that it was an impressive feat that now has Muzan at a disadvantage.
